item_17.note: Case: James-Sadler-MVA-4-07-2023. The client is James Sadler.

Between April and July 2025, counsel communications unfolded in the James Sadler v. Tafesse matter. The Whaley Law Firm’s W. Bryce Koon, Esq., wrote to Allison L. Rief, Attorney at Dilbeck and Myers, PLLC, with copies to Brooke Gallagher and the James Sadler MVA Filevine project email address ([EMAIL-11]). The initial excerpt in the record shows a July 23, 2025 message in which Koon followed up with counsel, requesting any update on the matter and signing off with his firm’s contact information and a standard confidentiality notice.

Earlier in the chain, on June 20, 2025, Allison Rief responded to a request to coordinate Mr. Sadler’s deposition, indicating she would confer with Mr. Tafesse and review calendars to find a workable time and would get back to the sender. In the same exchange, Bryce Koon replied (in a message dated June 20, 2025 at 11:26 AM) noting that, with written discovery apparently complete, they should provide potential deposition dates for Mr. Tafesse as soon as possible. He added that Mr. Sadler was widely available over the next two months if their calendars could accommodate coordinating his deposition as well, and he asked whether the parties would like to revisit informal negotiations before investing more time and resources in depositions. The message was sent from The Whaley Law Firm at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with the firm’s phone number as [PHONE-12] and fax as [PHONE-840], and it included the standard confidentiality notice.

On June 16, 2025, Allison Rief wrote that Mr. Tafesse was delayed by a Friday storm but had been by the office that day to verify his discovery responses; she attached the verification (discovery responses). Her signature block identified Dilbeck and Myers, PLLC, at 8005 Lyndon Centre Way, Suite 201, Louisville, KY 40222, with a telephone number of [PHONE-839] and fax [PHONE-15], and she included the customary confidentiality notice.

Earlier still, on June 13, 2025, Allison Rief had told Bryce that Tafesse would come in that afternoon to verify his discovery, and she expected to be able to send the verified discovery shortly thereafter. This message also carried the Dilbeck and Myers contact details and confidentiality notice.

A prior thread shows Bryce Koon’s June 11, 2025 email to Allison Rief (and others, with the James Sadler MVA Filevine address copied) asking when the parties might expect responses to their outstanding discovery requests. The June 11 message was followed by a June 3, 2025 note from Bryce asking counsel to advise when they may expect responses to the outstanding discovery requests, again with the Whaley Law Firm’s contact details and confidentiality notices.

There is an earlier exchange dated April 11, 2025 in the chain, in which Allison Rief replied with “ Appreciated – thank you” and Bryce Koon had sent a message to Allison earlier that day (12:16 PM) with copies to the Whaley firm and others; the details of that April 11 thread are partially captured in the record, confirming ongoing discovery-related communications before the June routine.

In sum, the record shows a coordinated effort from April through June 2025 to obtain and verify discovery materials, schedule and conduct depositions, and align the calendar for Mr. Tafesse’s deposition while also coordinating Mr. Sadler’s availability for deposition over the ensuing two-month window. The communications repeatedly reference written discovery as the trigger for moving toward depositions, the storm-related delay in Tafesse’s appearance, and the plan to revisit any informal negotiations if desired before expending further resources on depositions. The communications repeatedly carry the parties’ standard confidentiality notices and reference the same filevine project address for James Sadler’s MVA matter, along with the Whaley Law Firm’s and Dilbeck & Myers’ contact information.

item_22.note: This case note pertains to James Sadler in the matter captioned Sadler v. Tafesse (an April 7, 2023 motor vehicle accident), with the client identified as James Sadler. The document lines up a sequence of written discovery activities and deposition scheduling communications between counsel, culminating in a request for deposition dates for Mr. Tafesse and an invitation to revisit informal negotiations before further depositions.

On June 20, 2025, at 11:25:48 AM Eastern Time, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, wrote to Allison Rief, attorney for the defense at Dilbeck and Myers, PLLC. He noted that written discovery appeared to be complete and asked for potential dates for Mr. Tafesse’s deposition at the earliest convenience. He also indicated that Mr. Sadler is widely available over the next two months if the defense wished to coordinate his deposition as well. Koon asked to be advised whether the parties would like to revisit informal negotiations before committing additional time and resources to depositions. He provided his firm’s contact details: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; Phone [PHONE-25]; Fax [PHONE-26].

Earlier communications in the chain reflect ongoing discovery-related activity. On June 16, 2025, at 4:28 PM (noted as “4:28?PM” in the record), Allison L. Rief, attorney for Dilbeck and Myers, reported that a storm on Friday had delayed Mr. Tafesse, but he was able to come by the office that day to verify his discovery responses, which were attached to the message. Rief’s notice included firm contact details: Dilbeck and Myers, PLLC, 8005 Lyndon Centre Way, Suite 201, Louisville, KY 40222; Phone [PHONE-27]; Fax [PHONE-28]. The message also included standard confidentiality language.

On June 13, 2025, at 11:04 AM, Allison Rief had previously indicated that Mr. Tafesse would be coming in that afternoon to verify discovery, with the expectation that she would be able to forward the verified discovery soon afterwards. Her contact details and the firm’s information were included in that email as well.

On June 11, 2025, at 11:29 AM, Bryce Koon asked Allison Rief to advise when the parties might expect responses to outstanding discovery requests.

On June 3, 2025, at 11:44 AM, Bryce Koon followed up again, requesting an update on the discovery requests.

Earlier in the year, on April 11, 2025, there was a sequence concerning the drafting of discovery requests. Allison Rief wrote at 12:14 PM to indicate she had met with Mr. Tafesse that morning to answer discovery requests and requested that the opposing side send a Word document copy of their requests so she could draft responses. Bryce Koon replied at 12:16 PM, stating, “Good afternoon counsel, please see attached.” The message also noted that it had been cc’d to relevant recipients and included the dedicated Filevine project address for the Sadler MVA file. At 12:18 PM, Allison Rief replied, “Appreciated – thank you.”

Also on April 11, 2025, Bryce Koon sent a message at 12:16 PM stating, “Please see attached,” in reference to the discovery requests. This was followed by Allison’s 12:18 PM reply expressing appreciation.

In sum, the record reflects a coordinated effort across multiple weeks to complete discovery, verify discovery responses (including handling weather-related delays), and schedule depositions, with a current emphasis on identifying deposition dates for Mr. Tafesse and coordinating Mr. Sadler’s deposition within the next two months, while remaining open to informal settlement discussions before expending additional resources on depositions. The communications identify two law firms (The Whaley Law Firm and Dilbeck & Myers, PLLC), their respective representatives (Bryce Koon and Allison Rief), as well as the involved parties and project contact points (including the James Sadler MVA Filevine project address).

In the message, she stated that the client is still waiting to see whether he needs to go back on treatment, with a decision expected by July 19. Earlier that same day, Auto Medical Claims at State Farm replied with a standard message directing the recipient to open the attached documents for more claim information or next steps. The reply also included privacy and security guidance, advising not to include sensitive personal information (such as Social Security numbers, financial account numbers, driver’s license numbers, or health information) in emails, and suggesting the use of a secure email channel by contacting the claim associate if such information must be transmitted.

The reply further included boilerplate promotional text about receiving claim contact cards via text, encouraging the recipient to text AUTO to 62789 for an Auto claim card or to text HOME to 62789 for a Homeowners claim card. The message concluded with the usual signatures and boilerplate.

Signature details from Jessa Galosmo at Whaley Law Firm follow, including her phone number [PHONE-817] and fax number [PHONE-818].
